  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c03fe271-e6de-4c45-a0b6-1740ea52dfe4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7777903263928435944" style="display:none"><b>Tra-la-laaa! The wait is over! Dav Pilkey--ahem--we mean, George Beard and Harold Hutchins, the bestselling authors of THE ADVENTURES OF SUPER DIAPER BABY, are back with their second graphic novel!</b><br />Meet Ook and Gluk, the stars of this sensationally silly graphic novel from the creators of Captain Underpants! It's 500,001 BC, and Ook and Gluk's hometown of Caveland, Ohio, is under attack by an evil corporation from the future. When Ook, Gluk, and their little dinosaur pal Lily are pulled through a time portal to 2222, they discover a future world that's even more devastated than their own. Luckily, they find a friend in Master Wong, a martial arts instructor who trains them in the ways of kung fu. Now all they have to do is travel back in time 502,223 years and save the day!</span>

<div id="review_122012006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122012006" />
    <a title="Lars Guthrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/757602-lars-guthrie"><img alt="Lars Guthrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199816668p2/757602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122012006?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lars Guthrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lars Guthrie" href="/user/show/757602-lars-guthrie">Lars Guthrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122012006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7624416197653656645">I don't understand how people can disparage books that get kids reading. <br/><br/>If the grammar and spelling aren't always correct, isn't that in character for Mssrs. Beard and Hutchins? Aren't young readers discerning enough to realize that? Furthermore, could it not even help them to distinguish bad syntax and orthographics from good? <br/><br/>If the humor is low-brow, isn't that enticing to a certain audience (like me)?<br/><br/>And haven't we gotten over the 1950s censorial and snooty view of comic books yet? Hey, it'</span>
  <span id="freeText7624416197653656645" style="display:none">I don't understand how people can disparage books that get kids reading. <br /><br />If the grammar and spelling aren't always correct, isn't that in character for Mssrs. Beard and Hutchins? Aren't young readers discerning enough to realize that? Furthermore, could it not even help them to distinguish bad syntax and orthographics from good? <br /><br />If the humor is low-brow, isn't that enticing to a certain audience (like me)?<br /><br />And haven't we gotten over the 1950s censorial and snooty view of comic books yet? Hey, it's an art form, man.<br /><br />'Ook and Gluk' is fun, and funny! Really funny.<br /><br />I'm not the only one who thinks so. As of this date, 'O &amp; G' is a number one NY Times bestseller. Not on the Children's Books list. Graphic Books. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7624416197653656645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

(Excuse me while I practice my caveman language, aka Cavemonics.)<br/><br/>As with many a good cartoon work, this one has many layers, many which will only be understood and appreciated by the adult readers who give it a fair shot.</span>

<div id="review_124968470" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124968470" />
    <a title="Nicola Mansfield" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1682713-nicola-mansfield"><img alt="Nicola Mansfield" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510729582p2/1682713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124968470?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola Mansfield" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola Mansfield" href="/user/show/1682713-nicola-mansfield">Nicola Mansfield</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781407123882" href="/book/show/9086416-the-adventures-of-ook-and-gluk-kung-fu-cavemen-from-the-future-by-geor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124968470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17762161231894092476">Reason for Reading: My ds read aloud to me as his reader.<br/><br/>I received this book as an *extra* from Scholastic, along with one I had requested to review. I was not entirely impressed, I'm sorry to say. Neither I nor my children (up to 21 yo) have ever read a Dave Pilkey book and there has been a reason for that. I admit I do have certain la-di-da standards when it comes to what books I allow to pass through my children's hands and yes, you could call me a "book snob" in that sense. One of the thing</span>
  <span id="freeText17762161231894092476" style="display:none">Reason for Reading: My ds read aloud to me as his reader.<br /><br />I received this book as an *extra* from Scholastic, along with one I had requested to review. I was not entirely impressed, I'm sorry to say. Neither I nor my children (up to 21 yo) have ever read a Dave Pilkey book and there has been a reason for that. I admit I do have certain la-di-da standards when it comes to what books I allow to pass through my children's hands and yes, you could call me a "book snob" in that sense. One of the things that has always irritated me to no end is when parents, teachers, librarians, etc. will say about a child who consistently reads books with little to no literary merit is "At least they're reading!". My response to that has always been: You don't hand a child who won't eat his vegetables a box of cookies and say "At least they're eating!". It's the same thing, to me.<br /><br />But I have to admit, publicly, here and now, that I WAS WRONG about Dave Pilkey! At first glance through this book, I cringed at the purposeful spelling and grammar errors. I thought the story was silly (stupid, even) but then told myself the book is for 10yo boys not *ahem*yo mothers; the boys would love it. Wait a minute, *I* have a 10yo boy! Then I began to actually read the text and realized my 10 yo son would be able to read a good portion of this book. My son is autistic with several learning disabilities and at this point is reading easy readers. Here was a book, a thick book, with chapters, that was aimed at his age group that might actually excite him about reading. So I gave him the book, and while he did need a lot of help, he *could* read much of the book and LOVED the story. Every morning when we started our routine, he would say "I can't wait to read my book!" You don't know what music that was to this readaholic mum's ears! I usually give him a break from reading from his reader on Fridays, as he reads a story from an easy reader Bible that day but he was so upset to find "Ook and Gluk" missing that first Friday that he stormed off to get the book and happily read twice on Fridays from then on, without even thinking it was a chore!<br /><br />My son absolutely loved this book! Thought it was hilarious, loved the "flip-o-rama" pages and it is probably his favourite book *ever* right now. He was thrilled to see the page that said another Ook and Gluk book would be coming soon. Myself, I have to admit, it was funny and silly. I did laugh. The spelling and grammar errors were irksome but I got used to it and realize they made the book easier to read. My son was able to read some of the big words because they were misspelled, which gave him reading confidence. I don't intend to feed him a daily diet of Dave Pilkey but Dave is now welcome in our home and I intend to have him read the first graphic novel about the Diaper Baby in the not too distant future. Then I will finally go have a look at those darn Captain Underpants books! and check out the reading level. Thanks to OOk and Gluk, a mum learned a lesson and a boy found a book he was passionate to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17762161231894092476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1296931006" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296931006" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10943198-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587703738p2/10943198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296931006?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/10943198-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296931006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15043578222465971788">This book is simply adorable. If you are a fan of Captain Underpants, then you will love this little book! This book has action, drama, and romance. It is written by two 9-10 year old boys who are best friends in elementary school. This book is funny and gives you a break from reality. If you are like me and find yourself bored, you can pick up this book to literally be able to time-travel.<br/>In this book, the main characters are cavemen. Yes, you read that correctly. While you may be thinking abou</span>
  <span id="freeText15043578222465971788" style="display:none">This book is simply adorable. If you are a fan of Captain Underpants, then you will love this little book! This book has action, drama, and romance. It is written by two 9-10 year old boys who are best friends in elementary school. This book is funny and gives you a break from reality. If you are like me and find yourself bored, you can pick up this book to literally be able to time-travel.<br />In this book, the main characters are cavemen. Yes, you read that correctly. While you may be thinking about a Geico commercial right now, this is clearly not the case. Ook and Gluk are adorable and not really barbaric in anyway. As a matter of fact, they are pretty intelligent despite the way they talk.<br />While this book has plenty of misspellings, it is bound to keep you laughing or shaking your head at the stupidity. While I was reading this book, I found myself doing both things. But strangely enough, it works and works well. I wish that this series was more popular than what it is. It seems as if the Captain Underpants books are more popular and are more well-known. But believe it or not, this book was just as good if not better than Captain Underpants.<br />I found myself amused at Ook and Gluk trying to learn Kung-Fu. It seemed as if they really wanted a belt regardless of color, immediately. Ook and Glukâ€™s training for a year or so teaches patience and an ability to preserve regardless of circumstances. It shows that you must try in order to succeed.<br />This book also contains an adorable dinosaur. I love the dinosaur. Even though the poor dinosaur often gets sick from turning around, she is still adorable and helps Ook and Gluk to save the day. Plus, the dinosaur is a baby, which makes it even more adorable!<br />While this book may seem cheesy to some at first, it is really a great adventure. It has dinosaurs, cavemen, Kung-Fu, romance, and action. If you liked the Captain Underpants books (I did when I was growing up) then you are bound to love this book! My only wish for these books though, is colored pictures. I really want to see that sweet baby dinosaur in color! Awh!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15043578222465971788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6328414432222922800">There's stupid...and then there's stupid that works. Dav Pilkey* is a master of the second category. I read Captain Underpants back in the day (3rd grade, 4th grade, something like that)and loved it, so I tried out this spin-off book. The back of my mind picked up on the old cliches from that series (the maimed signs, "before we tell you that story, we have to tell you this story") and, while the artistic side of me was sad he wasn't more creative, it was like snuggling a much-loved teddy bear f</span>
  <span id="freeText6328414432222922800" style="display:none">There's stupid...and then there's stupid that works. Dav Pilkey* is a master of the second category. I read Captain Underpants back in the day (3rd grade, 4th grade, something like that)and loved it, so I tried out this spin-off book. The back of my mind picked up on the old cliches from that series (the maimed signs, "before we tell you that story, we have to tell you this story") and, while the artistic side of me was sad he wasn't more creative, it was like snuggling a much-loved teddy bear from childhood. Brilliant and tailored to kids, it was a good read, though I wouldn't give it the Nobel Prize or anything.<br />Heck, if a comic book can make a nineteen-year-old woman giggle at the line "Yeah, father of my BUTT!", it's a huge akomplushmint...er, accomplishment.<br /><br />*with a name like that, you've got to have a sense of humor</span>

<div id="review_2518058081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2518058081" />
    <a title="James Crawford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86267683-james-crawford"><img alt="James Crawford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536015792p2/86267683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2518058081?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Crawford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Crawford" href="/user/show/86267683-james-crawford">James Crawford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86267683-james-crawford?shelf=dav-pilkey">dav-pilkey</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2518058081&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2518058081" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2708442139786840138">A great book that came out of nowhere about two cavemen, ook and gluk featuring dinosaurs and time travel. I love this book for so many reasons. But this is already getting kinda long so I will just tell you some of the good parts. Ook and Gluk training, a running gag about names that sound familiar, and a sequel that will probably come out in the middle of nowhere hopefully because it's been a lot of years. Anyways it was a great book that I loved to read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934126639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1067477265648307139">Similar to Diary of a Wimpy Kid, “Ook and Gluk” has a lot of goofy pictures and entertaining dialogue. Ook and Gluk, two cavemen in 500,001 BC, find a time-traveler from the future that’s coming back and trying to steal their natural resources. They travel to the future and learn kung-fu, fighting off the bad guys with ridiculous and humorous situations, saving the day. This book is an example of a graphic novel, written in a style like a comic book, containing various elements like panels and s</span>
  <span id="freeText1067477265648307139" style="display:none">Similar to Diary of a Wimpy Kid, “Ook and Gluk” has a lot of goofy pictures and entertaining dialogue. Ook and Gluk, two cavemen in 500,001 BC, find a time-traveler from the future that’s coming back and trying to steal their natural resources. They travel to the future and learn kung-fu, fighting off the bad guys with ridiculous and humorous situations, saving the day. This book is an example of a graphic novel, written in a style like a comic book, containing various elements like panels and sound effects. It’s recommended by the ALSC for grades 3-5, but I’ve known 2nd graders to also enjoy this book. The humor is more suitable for the younger end of the spectrum, and is similar to Pilkey’s other books, like “Captain Underpants.” <br /><br />I would use this to encourage readers that might otherwise be intimidated by, or uninterested in, various types of books. Its structure is very different from other mediums, and for that reason it can help support reading with learners that struggle; research supports the use of a variety of reading materials to boost higher average reading scores. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1067477265648307139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077657271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14663982967134531970">I never expected to read, much less review, a graphic novel about kung fu-fighting cavemen authored by fictional characters, but for a long time I did not expect to be a parent, either, and here we are.<br/><br/>The book is a spin-off of Pilkey's popular Captain Underpants novels, and its title sums up its plot pretty well. The lives of two cavemen who look remarkably like our Underpants protagonists are interrupted when a businessman from the future comes to steal all their resources. They travel through</span>
  <span id="freeText14663982967134531970" style="display:none">I never expected to read, much less review, a graphic novel about kung fu-fighting cavemen authored by fictional characters, but for a long time I did not expect to be a parent, either, and here we are.<br /><br />The book is a spin-off of Pilkey's popular Captain Underpants novels, and its title sums up its plot pretty well. The lives of two cavemen who look remarkably like our Underpants protagonists are interrupted when a businessman from the future comes to steal all their resources. They travel through the time portal, learn kung fu, and take the matter into their own hands.<br /><br />There is probably something worth saying about race in this book, which positions "ancient" Asian philosophy and martial arts as a future technology, but, really, the point of the story is to grab kids' attention, get them reading, and maybe develop some thoughts about social justice. My own kid, who is new to chapter books, loved having so many pictures on every page, and like I say of all his faves, I am sure we'll be rereading this one again and again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14663982967134531970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer644413624990008281">Ook Schadowski and Gluk Jones, two cool cavemen from prehistorical Caveland, Ohio found out that Chief Goppernopper wants to marry Ook's sister, Gak, but refused. A few days later, their hometown is under attack by J. P. Goppernopper from the future. Ex-Chief Goppernopper meets his future self and hired, so the Goppernoppers from the Past and Future came along to destroy Caveland.<br/><br/>Meanwhile, Ook and Gluk, who are now slaves, hides at Master Wong's School of Kung-Fu and met their teacher, Master W</span>
  <span id="freeText644413624990008281" style="display:none">Ook Schadowski and Gluk Jones, two cool cavemen from prehistorical Caveland, Ohio found out that Chief Goppernopper wants to marry Ook's sister, Gak, but refused. A few days later, their hometown is under attack by J. P. Goppernopper from the future. Ex-Chief Goppernopper meets his future self and hired, so the Goppernoppers from the Past and Future came along to destroy Caveland.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Ook and Gluk, who are now slaves, hides at Master Wong's School of Kung-Fu and met their teacher, Master Wong and his daughter, Lan. He teaches not just academics, creativity and taking care of the environment, but also Kung-Fu to the boys. They learned for years and years until they grew up as men earning their black belts from him, and they taught about one important question - Who is the Greatest Man? <br /><br />Ook and Gluk fights against the bad guys, including the Goppernoppers, all the way to save the past and the future.<br /><br />With trademark misspelled words, sign gags, action packed Flip-O-Ramas and full of laffs, plus a guide to learn Cavemonics (Caveman Language), this is surely an awesome 3-star graphic novel from George Beard and Harold Hutchins.</span>

<div id="review_136343139" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136343139" />
    <a title="Leslie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1455162-leslie"><img alt="Leslie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566257491p2/1455162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136343139?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/1455162-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136343139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2494700556621654331">Christmas present for my little caveman. Unlike Captain Underpants and Ricky Ricotta and His MIghty Robot, this Dav Pilkey creation is entirely in graphic novel form. For us old fogies, that means it's a long comic book. One thing I noticed right away is the intentional misspellings that are supposed to make the book feel like two little boys wrote it. Well, it bothered me a little, and my Asperger's son some too. But not enough to not buy the book! We're just so happy Dav Pilkey wrote something</span>
  <span id="freeText2494700556621654331" style="display:none">Christmas present for my little caveman. Unlike Captain Underpants and Ricky Ricotta and His MIghty Robot, this Dav Pilkey creation is entirely in graphic novel form. For us old fogies, that means it's a long comic book. One thing I noticed right away is the intentional misspellings that are supposed to make the book feel like two little boys wrote it. Well, it bothered me a little, and my Asperger's son some too. But not enough to not buy the book! We're just so happy Dav Pilkey wrote something else. Having said that, I must add that it's not as funny as the other two series. My son did lol a few times with this one but no seizure like fits of hysterical shrieking laughter like he does over his favorite, Captain Freaking Underpants. Sigh. We're all so jaded. At this point, if Pilkey wrote the text for toilet paper packaging, I'd buy it. My son reads anything by this Pilkey person and that means he's getting this idea filed away in his little boy brain that reading is cool, funny and worth the effort. Works for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2494700556621654331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1244314469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Amber Hurlbert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39243695-amber-hurlbert"><img alt="Amber Hurlbert" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1244314469?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber Hurlbert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber Hurlbert" href="/user/show/39243695-amber-hurlbert">Amber Hurlbert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39243695-amber-hurlbert?shelf=2015-children-s-literature">2015-children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244314469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6259033763217935299">"The adventures of Ook and Gluk : Kung-fu cavemen from the future" is a graphic novel. I am not as into graphic novels, but this was a silly/fun book that students may like. <br/><br/>Text-self: I would ask students to think of their best friend that they like to have fun with. They can share their favorite thing to do with their best friend if they would like. <br/><br/>Text-world: I would ask the students to think what life would be like if there were two cavemen alive today and how they would react to the world </span>
  <span id="freeText6259033763217935299" style="display:none">"The adventures of Ook and Gluk : Kung-fu cavemen from the future" is a graphic novel. I am not as into graphic novels, but this was a silly/fun book that students may like. <br /><br />Text-self: I would ask students to think of their best friend that they like to have fun with. They can share their favorite thing to do with their best friend if they would like. <br /><br />Text-world: I would ask the students to think what life would be like if there were two cavemen alive today and how they would react to the world we live in. I would also ask the students to think what life would have been like in 500,001 BC like in the book. <br /><br />Text-text: Captain underpants is a book by the same author, so if students like this book, they would probably like those. I would find another book about cavemen to be a twin text, and compare it to this book. A non-fiction book, or a book about theories on real cavemen, would be fun for the students to read with this as well, so they can see what they think could be realistic. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6259033763217935299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129686938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129686938" />
    <a title="Abby Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53329-abby-johnson"><img alt="Abby Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484521399p2/53329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129686938?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby Johnson" href="/user/show/53329-abby-johnson">Abby Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129686938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9819870945372403151">Ook and Gluk are cavemen in the year 500,001 BC. When an evil corporation from the year 2222 AD shows up and starts pillaging their resources and enslaving the cavepeople, Ook and Gluk head into the future to save the day. It's a madcap action-adventure comic book with tons of potty humor. Written by Dav Pilkey as if it had been written by 2 fourth-grade boys, the comic is rife with misspellings and chock full of fun. I wouldn't be surprised if it inspires young readers to create their own comic</span>
  <span id="freeText9819870945372403151" style="display:none">Ook and Gluk are cavemen in the year 500,001 BC. When an evil corporation from the year 2222 AD shows up and starts pillaging their resources and enslaving the cavepeople, Ook and Gluk head into the future to save the day. It's a madcap action-adventure comic book with tons of potty humor. Written by Dav Pilkey as if it had been written by 2 fourth-grade boys, the comic is rife with misspellings and chock full of fun. I wouldn't be surprised if it inspires young readers to create their own comics. <br /><br />Okay, I admit that I had the knee-jerk grownup reaction when I first opened this book: "Ugh, all the words are misspelled! When does the REAL book begin?" <br /><br />Yeah, and then I let go of that and just had a monstrously fun reading experience. It's books like this that turn kids ON to reading. This will be a super choice for fans of Captain Underpants and silly, funny books. <br /><br />More on the blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.abbythelibrarian.com/2010/11/adventures-of-ook-and-gluk-giveaway.html">http://www.abbythelibrarian.com/2010/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9819870945372403151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2344386-caitlin?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252984597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3936824311443695293">I read this one after a recommendation from one of my students (7th grade boy), who could not put the book down and said it was "so funny." I just could not make it past page 50 (I try to follow <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/67412.Nancy_Pearl' title='Nancy Pearl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nancy Pearl</a>'s 'rule of 50'--if the book is not grabbing you after 50 pages, set it aside!). While I appreciate some graphic novels, this one was absolutely awful. Clearly, some kids will like it. I can imagine kids (maybe grade 3 and up?) looking for an 'easy read' (or very reluctant readers) reading thi</span>
  <span id="freeText3936824311443695293" style="display:none">I read this one after a recommendation from one of my students (7th grade boy), who could not put the book down and said it was "so funny." I just could not make it past page 50 (I try to follow <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/67412.Nancy_Pearl" title="Nancy Pearl" rel="nofollow noopener">Nancy Pearl</a>'s 'rule of 50'--if the book is not grabbing you after 50 pages, set it aside!). While I appreciate some graphic novels, this one was absolutely awful. Clearly, some kids will like it. I can imagine kids (maybe grade 3 and up?) looking for an 'easy read' (or very reluctant readers) reading this one with gusto. Terrible drawings, pubescent humor, and a just plain silly plot made me put Ook and Gluk back on the shelf.</span>

          </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443521594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3231538329200243298">In this hilarious graphic novel, Ook and Gluk are two cavemen who are sent to the future where they learn Kungfu, and set out to stop the evil Goppernopper from taking over the world and enslaving all of the people.<br/><br/><br/>Ages 4-9<br/><br/>Many readers will enjoy the graphic novel format of this book. It has black and white illustrations that are funny and include dinosaurs, caveman, laser guns, and kungfu; a long list that of things that kids 4-9 love! Furthermore, it is full of bathroom humor that all kids wil</span>
  <span id="freeText3231538329200243298" style="display:none">In this hilarious graphic novel, Ook and Gluk are two cavemen who are sent to the future where they learn Kungfu, and set out to stop the evil Goppernopper from taking over the world and enslaving all of the people.<br /><br /><br />Ages 4-9<br /><br />Many readers will enjoy the graphic novel format of this book. It has black and white illustrations that are funny and include dinosaurs, caveman, laser guns, and kungfu; a long list that of things that kids 4-9 love! Furthermore, it is full of bathroom humor that all kids will find hilarious.<br /><br />I think a teacher could use this as a way to motivate reluctant readers. Also, I think it would be great for boys. A teacher could use the same format and have kids create their own graphic novel, using illustrations and simple sentences.<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_152837097" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152837097" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1368894-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436839067p2/1368894.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152837097?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/1368894-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1368894-jessica?shelf=grade-4-5-6-classroom-books">grade-4-5-6-classroom-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152837097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6467466203702329902">I don't care if I sound like an old, O.C.D., English teacher and book snob; because I am. While I could go off on a rant about this...I don't approve of nine year olds shouting SUCKAAASSSS! and I think the constant over-played misspellings just encourages my kids to write like fools...I'll let it go. One word says it best: DUMB. On that note...any goofy little boy will love it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2674032213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2674032213" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4326071-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597352802p2/4326071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2674032213?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/4326071-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545385770" href="/book/show/10683697-the-adventures-of-ook-and-gluk">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2674032213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6813244777423486975">I don't make any secret that I really love Dav Pilkey's books. People willing to see past the crude drawings and seemingly childish humor often find a story with heart and WAY more diverse characters than I ever knew were in these books.<br/><br/>What's <i>The Adventures of Ook and Gluk [...]</i> about? What it says on the tin: Two cavemen living in prehistoric Ohio get into shenanigans. They begin the story by irking their chief (here, ofc, spelled cheif) Goppernopper, as he and his "gards" direct them back to </span>
  <span id="freeText6813244777423486975" style="display:none">I don't make any secret that I really love Dav Pilkey's books. People willing to see past the crude drawings and seemingly childish humor often find a story with heart and WAY more diverse characters than I ever knew were in these books.<br /><br />What's <i>The Adventures of Ook and Gluk [...]</i> about? What it says on the tin: Two cavemen living in prehistoric Ohio get into shenanigans. They begin the story by irking their chief (here, ofc, spelled cheif) Goppernopper, as he and his "gards" direct them back to their respective houses to be chided, he falls in love with Ook's sister, Gak. He demands she marry him, otherwise bad things will happen to Ook and Gluk, and Gak agrees, seeing no possible other way to help them.<br /><br />Luckily our heroes are a little more savvy. They plan to disrupt Gak's wedding and run off Gopernopper for good. They succeed, due heavily to Mog Mog, a t-rex they've been antagonizing most of their lives. As Goppernopper leaves the village and contemplates just how much he can't stand Ook and Gluk, he runs into a <b>lot</b> of big machines tearing down trees and bottling the water, and thus meets his descendant future!Goppernopper.<br /><br />future!Goppernobber explains to original recipe Goppernopper that they invented a time machine to come back and clean the older world out of resources since the future is dying and has no fresh resources. f!Goppernopper takes ORGoppernopper to the future to see this distasterousness and ORGoppernopper suggests one <b>teensie</b> improvement: taking his former villagers and enslaving them.<br /><br />Both Goppernoppers go back to the past with mechanical dinosaurs and tell the residents that, surprise!, you've got a fantastic job opportunity working for Amazon of the distant future. Of course Ook and Gluk don't stand for it, and they escape, along with Mog Mog's child with who they've made friends, and go from the year 500,001BC to 2222AD to stop the Goppernoppers and have adventures.<br /><br />And I loved every second. One thing I really like about some YA/MG/Children's books is that I get to shut down and not think critically, but not in a bad way. Just "stop! Let the author tell the story!" way. That happens here, although I did go "but messing up the resources of the past will DEFINITELY mess up the resources of the future! Unless this is a stable time loop... Or that messing up the past is what CAUSES the future to be so wonky!" But I'm also completely aware that the book isn't meant to be taken so seriously or have such an intricate plot.<br /><br />It's meant to get little kids reading with humor on their level (and a few jokes for the older readers slipped in; peep the "speak like a caveman" section), and I think it does a wonderful job. Yeah, the art and grammar may be crude, but I've always thought that nothing had to be absolutely perfect to be enjoyable.<br /><br />I eagerly look forward to Dav Pilkey's future releases, I got almost a whole collection of his and I consider it money and time well spent, and if you give his books a try, you can knock one out in an hour.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6813244777423486975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LqL0yHqrzKDiMC01uL8qa9K7PuE6Zibi8poT/a2yR9P/n6peTGENpKdW+ZtsXd+TQ6DNPE68wGiaMuWafHh+tQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w3vhWrH2OptV6K6ZYlNd5+Z5T47xMA+1JD6ImUVsaMkSRr/Mhzz7nxCOeje2sagfd2K8U4Xq6T9Mln7+lKZRrw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7327754916147654230">David "Dav" Pilkey (b. March 4, 1966), is a popular children's author and artist. Pilkey is best known as the author and illustrator of the Captain Underpants book series. He lives near Seattle, Washington with his wife, Sayuri.<br/><br/></span>
